<div id="review_244324309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244324309" />
    <a title="Searock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6641663-searock"><img alt="Searock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396402019p2/6641663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244324309?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Searock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Searock" href="/user/show/6641663-searock">Searock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6641663-searock?shelf=fabulous-in-every-way">fabulous-in-every-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6641663-searock?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244324309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18432154483723952165">5 stars for the <b>utter wonder</b> I felt while reading this book! It was filled with <i>all kinds</i> of win!!<br/><br/>Prepare to be gushed upon!!<br/><br/>I had never closed a book and then flipped it back to the beginning for a second read until now :) I have a third read planned within a month of my first reading. That may be one definition of <b>obsession</b>.<br/><br/>This is my first Kristen Ashley and I loved it, so am currently hacking away at her back list… nom, nom, nom. I'm also looking forward to her new releases. KA is prolific a</span>
  <span id="freeText18432154483723952165" style="display:none">5 stars for the <b>utter wonder</b> I felt while reading this book! It was filled with <i>all kinds</i> of win!!<br /><br />Prepare to be gushed upon!!<br /><br />I had never closed a book and then flipped it back to the beginning for a second read until now :) I have a third read planned within a month of my first reading. That may be one definition of <b>obsession</b>.<br /><br />This is my first Kristen Ashley and I loved it, so am currently hacking away at her back list… nom, nom, nom. I'm also looking forward to her new releases. KA is prolific and churning them out faster than a one-armed paper hanger. *happy face*<br /><br /><b>I highly recommend this book and urge you not to miss the forest for the trees in regard to the writing!</b><br /><br />Yes, this is an indie author and yeah, she's got an amateur style and yep, there are lots of writing rules that are being broken (long, meandering sentences, "I-strain", etc.), but for this book, I say "fu*k the rules"! <br /><br />The style is totally fitting for this wonderful plot about the completely alpha, politically inappropriate, bad-boy hero, Tate, versus the oh-so-successful and rule-abiding, nice, bad-guy, Brad (pronounced: <i>Newman</i>). <br /><br />The author also breaks the rules of the 350 magical wrap-up and gives us approximately *mumble, mumble, carry the one* 600 pages or more (!) of active dialog and ever-unfolding storyline. <br /><br />The author doesn't give us the hero with a heart of gold, no sirree! She gives us Tate who is such a jerk (!) that he badmouths our leading lady in a painful, rejecting way and I for one thoroughly enjoyed the grudge match that ensued! I luuuuuvved getting behind the heroine in those early scenes and seeing her hold her own against an arrogant and cold (although quite swoon-worthy) Tate. Even after our Hero becomes slightly more heroic, he continues to act like an ass and Lauren tells him at one point **spoiler quote** (edited Jan 10 to switch to this similar, but not quite so spoilerish quote):<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>“God, if he wasn’t so handsome, strong, sometimes sweet, didn’t have a Harley, that beard, a tendency to play with my hair, didn’t look so good in jeans and wasn’t so danged good in bed, he would seriously not be worth it.”</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />**end spoiler quote**<br /><br />Thank God I didn’t miss any of this story due to what a publisher might do to it (yikes!). I found a comfort in the streaming, detailed writing style the author used. It kept me oriented in the story at all times and allowed me to truly get lost in it. I never had to grope around in the dark, ever. Those details were the cream in my story latte! I even got to the point that if she hadn’t mentioned what she was wearing, I went into bad stalker mode and wondered, “What are you wearing right now?”<br /><br />Seriously, <b>what trees</b>? <br /><br />I obsessively read this book and it still took me four days- this baby is huuuuge. <b>I'm grinning just thinking about this reading experience</b>. I chuckled and guffawed and I even cried (so rare!). I stopped a few times just to say aloud, <i>"Wow, this is good"</i>. I haven't done that since I read Ivory's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1130878.Beast" title="Beast by Judith Ivory" rel="nofollow noopener">Beast</a>.<br /><br />This story may have the best opening chapter I've read in a long, long time (ever?). Then it just gets better from there. <br /><br />The lead (Lauren) was looking for "nothing special" just something "real". This story captures her journey and the paradox of it brilliantly. It’s organic, utterly relatable, twisty-turny, revelatory, engrossing, and delightful. This was designated for my keeper shelf before I got through the first half!<br /><br /><b>The last third feels like a "harvest" and begins to bear fruit</b>. I use that word because there are many secondary characters that have their own little story arcs. When one is used to reading fairly boilerplate romances, this felt decadent and was utterly satisfying. I was going to mention some secondary arcs for the sake of nostalgia, but once I got started, I had to stop because there were too many! <br /><br />The side characters were integral and wonderfully portrayed. There were no throwaways and <b>just thinking about them makes me happy</b> *waves to Deke, Wendy, Ned and Betty, Pop and Stella, Twyla, and even Wanda at the Deluxe Home Store*. There’s even more than I mentioned here and gosh darn it, I missed em’ as soon as I closed the book!<br /><br />There is an intimacy, a connectedness that Laurie develops with many, if not all, of the characters in the story and it added a soul-satisfying element to the experience for me as a reader. KA’s writing is simply engaging. I too, was connected to Laurie and her story (so connected I didn’t want to let go) and it made her story charming and magical for me. I am sounding like this is a wee fairy tale but <b>it is not at all!</b> It’s got a raunchy, gritty surface and there’s a lot of crass talk, but the sweet, yummy, hopeful, happy, frosting-in-the-middle shows through the whole time. <br /><br />Things I Loved:<br /><br />I loved that the author goofed around with the timeline. Some reviewers felt it was confusing or choppy, but I adored starting a scene with something rather teasing like, **big spoiler** Laurie gets a call from Wood and they make a plan for “later” (what!) and then goes back to explain for the reader’s benefit that Tate’s been gone a month with no word, and that all these interesting and surprising things occurred (shenanigans!) in the meantime which led to Wood and Laurie… you know, sort of, um… ** end major spoiler**. It made the narrative more interesting to me and has become a bit of a signature for KA. It might need a bit of improvement so as too never be confusing, but I like the device. <br /><br />I loved how beautifully the author portrays that the golf-shirt-wearing, suburb-dwelling executive, ex-husband who had a nasty habit of chipping away at the heroine’s self-image is exponentially more dangerous than the brash, volatile, politically incorrect, biker who drops the f-bomb anywhere, anytime, but would give his life for the woman he loves and for his family. The theme is repeated when Tate gives a beautiful explanation about the two kinds of women who “get under your skin”. <br /><br />I loved the themes of flowers, food, sleep, sweet dreams, and the evolution of Tate’s house with its upgrades and improvements and décor. I enjoyed watching it turn from a “stuck in the past” bachelor pad to something dreamy.<br /><br />I loved that this book gives you another set of words and phrases that take on special meaning (like it's own mini-language): Dick territory vs, chick territory, moist factor 500, Babe!, and like 20 other unique, little quirky sayings.<br /><br /><b>This is a book that begs for re-reads</b> (like an investment that keeps giving). Re-reading this 1st person narrative changed the experience to an omniscient one. It may not be true for all first person books, but in Sweet Dreams, a ton of information was revealed in the unfolding narrative so going back to the beginning and reading with all-knowing eyes made it a totally unique adventure.<br /><br />Of course it isn’t a perfect book. There are some conversations between the leads in which Lauren interrupts Tate like 10 times. I think the author tends toward long, sometimes meandering, one-sided dialog, so when Tate is doing that, some attempt for Lauren to get a word in edgewise is understandable, but yeesh, let’s just say it was often, and a lot and often (alot). There were times when it felt authentic and others times it pulled me out of the story and I stared at the writing. <br /><br />I could have done without the typical plot device which was **major, major, giving-away-the-end-spoiler** <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the typical kidnapped h, yada, yada, yada, rescued by the H and bam, there’s your HEA. Ugh. I know it works and its cool and all, but ugh, Laurie didn’t need to almost die for this HEA! It could have been done without it. Oh well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>** end of major, major spoiler.<br /><br />End of gush!<br /><br />So yeah, if you’re looking for a haiku or something, this isn’t it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18432154483723952165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=sexy-alpha-male">sexy-alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=there-is-kids-involved">there-is-kids-involved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804260367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6799155502027864251"><b><u>Second re-read: 12.08.2019</u>:</b> <br/>Am I the only one who gets annoyed by all the use of ‘baby’, ‘darlin/darling’, ‘honey’, ‘babe’, and so forth that KA uses in EVERY book? Also, this book takes <i>forever</i> to read, so I don't get why I even started it. I skimmed a little, but not much, surprisingly, considering it's damned long and barely anything happens. And the constant cutting a sentence in order to make it more ‘alpha’ is also quite annoying. Overall, I don't understand myself at all. Tate's hot thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText6799155502027864251" style="display:none"><b><u>Second re-read: 12.08.2019</u>:</b> <br>Am I the only one who gets annoyed by all the use of ‘baby’, ‘darlin/darling’, ‘honey’, ‘babe’, and so forth that KA uses in EVERY book? Also, this book takes <i>forever</i> to read, so I don't get why I even started it. I skimmed a little, but not much, surprisingly, considering it's damned long and barely anything happens. And the constant cutting a sentence in order to make it more ‘alpha’ is also quite annoying. Overall, I don't understand myself at all. Tate's hot though. But KA's women are too boring.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>Re-read: 05.03.2017</u>:</b> <br><b>I really don't get why I started re-reading this book</b>. Nor do I get why I actually finished re-reading it. As you all know, I don't really get alone with <b>KA</b>'s female characters, though <b>Lauren ‘Laurie’ ‘Ace’ Grahame</b> (42) ain't all that bad (but not the greatest either, but we get along), however I <b>do love</b> her male characters (mostly) and <b>Tatum ‘Tate’ ‘Captain’ ‘Buck’ Jackson</b> (44) is a character worth loving. He's hot, sexy, sweet, yet full of temper and has a mean mouth but honest and bold, commanding, and typical <b>KA</b> alpha male. As far as the story goes, it is alright. It's nothing special, but still alright. I specially adore Tate with <b>Jonas ‘Bub’ Jackson</b> (10). And I have to be honest - I was brought to (tears) teary eyes at some point in the book, even though I've read it before.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>First read review</u>:</b> <br><b>Back at it again with my mixed feelings...</b><br>Now, I only have like two-three problems with this book: <br>→ <b>1)</b> The ages of the characters = too close to my parents and it just feels a bit <i>wrong</i> for me.<br>→ <b>2)</b> The book is <i>way</i> too long, considering not much happened.<br>→ <b>3)</b> The book was dragged out, not much happened and did I mention it was long?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You’re safe, Lauren,” he murmured and my eyes came back to his.<br>“You weren’t safe with him but, honey, swear to God, you’re safe with me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The story was dragged out, nothing exciting was happening, and it was pretty much the same old, same old: <i>all the men wanting the woman who thought she was nothing special</i>. I get it, it fun, and cute but it got me bored. I don't like being bored, specially when reading a long book. I like not wanting to stop reading, I like when my heart skips a beat and I find myself glued to every sentence. Did that happen here? No, for the most part I was wondering how long I had left of the book. I'm not saying it was bad, quite the opposite, it was just too long for me to actually enjoy it. I loose interest. Anyway, at least KA is really, and I mean <i>really</i> good at writing sexy, macho, alpha males ;) Oh! And is it just me, or do KA really love the words <i>honey, babe, baby,</i> and <i>sweetheart</i>? Perhaps a little too much?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You want sweet dreams, lose the attitude and you might find I'll give you reason to have them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487806562i/22053171.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Contemporary Romance<br><b>Series</b>: - (Standalone?) Series, Book Two <br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, in a way - h was seeing someone else when having sex with H. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Tatum Jackson<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Yes.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Sure.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - No.<br><b>Rating</b> - 2.5/3 stars.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_353453912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353453912" />
    <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads"><img alt="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578074503p2/8524618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353453912?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads">Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353453912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14860962305839100266">This book was <b>AMAZING. <br/><br/>OH MY GOSH.</b> <br/><br/>I <b>LOVED</b> every minute of it. Tate, Laurie, Jim Billy, Wood, Jonas, Krys, Bubba, Sunny, Shambles, ALL of them. I cannot get enough. She creates so many different types of characters and all are so unique and breathtaking.<br/><br/>What I think really gets me about KA'S books is that when I'm done reading I feel like I <b>KNOW</b> her characters inside and out. She makes them come to life, she gives them a body and a soul with her words. There is no detail left out, no thought, or</span>
  <span id="freeText14860962305839100266" style="display:none">This book was <b>AMAZING. <br /><br />OH MY GOSH.</b> <br /><br />I <b>LOVED</b> every minute of it. Tate, Laurie, Jim Billy, Wood, Jonas, Krys, Bubba, Sunny, Shambles, ALL of them. I cannot get enough. She creates so many different types of characters and all are so unique and breathtaking.<br /><br />What I think really gets me about KA'S books is that when I'm done reading I feel like I <b>KNOW</b> her characters inside and out. She makes them come to life, she gives them a body and a soul with her words. There is no detail left out, no thought, or emotion not felt. She touches on <b>EVERYTHING.</b> She gives it to you. It's unreal. It really is... With all the so-so reads out there, this is a <b>REAL</b> book, written by an author who gives her readers a <b>FULL BODY</b> experience. <br /><br />I swear, I always know, even if the book or the characters aren't my thing, my taste, that Kristen Ashley is going to give me a <b>SOLID</b> novel. Nothing half-assed. <br /><br />It will be <b>PURE GOLD.</b> <br /><br />Gah! And another things that KA does best is even in the most painful moments, the moments with so much angst, she manages to find a way to soothe you, to give you a laugh, or a tummy dip, or a smile, just something. I felt that in this book. <br /><br />Tate was a jerk, yet even in his most douchey moments, he made me laugh and feeelllllll! And Laurie... what can I say?! The best. She was sweet but feisty. <br /><br />GOOD LORD! This was another perfect KA read.<br /><br />Overall, I'm on cloud nine. I'm going into Lady Luck because all I wanna do is read KA. She's a go to, auto click author, who I trust to deliver a well written, emotional and sexy read time and time again. <br /><br /><b>MORE</b> than 5 stars here. Tate + Laurie = Perfection! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14860962305839100266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_275523329" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275523329" />
    <a title="Lady Heather " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2736715-lady-heather"><img alt="Lady Heather " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418473645p2/2736715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275523329?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Heather " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Heather " href="/user/show/2736715-lady-heather">Lady Heather </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">contemporary romance,chick-lit, bad-ass alpha males</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=best-series">best-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=love-the-author-a-must-buy">love-the-author-a-must-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2736715-lady-heather?shelf=kristen-ashley">kristen-ashley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275523329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12625298187940132944"><i>First read: February 10-14, 2012</i> <br/><br/>" And when he spoke, his voice was near to a growl.<br/> "A woman gets under your skin, the kind of woman that feeds the muscle, the bone, the soul, no replacing that.....but once you have that, there's no replacing it."<br/> I stared at him and he stared back. <br/> Then I whispered, "Tate-"<br/> but stopped speaking when his hand moved and his thumb tweaked the diamond he'd slid on my finger six weeks before.<br/> "No replacing it," he repeated on his own whisper."<br/><br/>- favourite quote in </span>
  <span id="freeText12625298187940132944" style="display:none"><i>First read: February 10-14, 2012</i> <br><br>" And when he spoke, his voice was near to a growl.<br> "A woman gets under your skin, the kind of woman that feeds the muscle, the bone, the soul, no replacing that.....but once you have that, there's no replacing it."<br> I stared at him and he stared back. <br> Then I whispered, "Tate-"<br> but stopped speaking when his hand moved and his thumb tweaked the diamond he'd slid on my finger six weeks before.<br> "No replacing it," he repeated on his own whisper."<br><br>- favourite quote in the book and I love how the author refers to being 'under your skin', and 'feeding the muscle, bone, and soul' .... life sustenance. <br><br>Loved this book. Loved Lauren and Tate. <br>I loved that the author didn't ever change Tate's wickedly, TOTALLY BAD-ASS, Biker-dude, Alpha-Male attitude... and that Lauren had to 'learn' the lingo, learn how to be a 'biker-babe' without changing who she was...and that her light never got extinguished, but that she 'lit up'...sometimes literally.<br><br>....*sigh*... basically A LOT of LOVE for this book.<br><br><i>Re-read: September 1, 2013</i> <b>Still 5 stars</b><br><br>Okay, so I just finished re-reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11227041.The_Gamble__Colorado_Mountain___1_" title="The Gamble (Colorado Mountain, #1) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gamble</a>(AND LOVED IT!) I started my re-read of this book on my way back from Ottawa yesterday, and finished it at 4:30 am this morning. <br>LOVED Tate and Lauren!<br><br>The only thing that kinda bothered me about this story (and I remember feeling the same way the first time I read this book) was why did it seem impossible for Lauren to have a child with Tate at 42-43 years old. <br>She said she wanted children (and nothing against Jonas). I know the risk is higher and all, but it was not impossible (and they never seemed to use protection right from the start).<br>... just a thought<br><br><i>Third re-read: August 1, 2014</i><br><br>This is the picture Dorsey posted on 'twitter' that inspired me to re-read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11227040.Sweet_Dreams__Colorado_Mountain___2_" title="Sweet Dreams (Colorado Mountain, #2) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Sweet Dreams</a><br><br><a href="http://s1095.photobucket.com/user/hebbies37/media/review%20pics%20for%20me/tate.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406894283i/10613726._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo tate.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Thank you, Dorsey! I really enjoyed this story..again!<br><br>Fourth re-read September 1-2, 2017<br><br>It's been a couple of years since I read this book and it was refreshing to discover that I had no recall of the story (so it was like I was reading it for the first time). <br>What an amazing treat to re-read this story!<br>Once again I was brought to the small town of Carnal, Colorado where the town is filled with unique characters.<br>A town filled with uber-alpha, domineering, possessive male bikers/bar owners/bounty hunters and strong, smart, sassy, funny awesome female leads.<br>This is one of the first books I read by Kristen Ashley, and it's the reason I became such a huge fan of her storytelling and amazing voice.<br>Loved this re-read!<br><br><b>Fifth re-read: December 11-13, 2018</b><br><br>I friggn LOVE Tate and Lauren!<br>I forgot how much I love visiting the <i>"Colorada Mountain Men"</i>!<br>Once again, an amazing re-read. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12625298187940132944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SHxfRx5YE+FG7a70JKFvuHontVPeT5W6FibZ4/eEzXEj++9T2jjkaaD64farAk8ekbcbLZ6eLdaEEeA9MIOi3g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer15433449007212965080">Kristen Ashley was born in Gary, Indiana, USA. She nearly killed her mother and herself making it into the world, seeing as she had the umbilical cord wrapped around her neck (already attempting to accessorise and she hadn't taken her first breath!). <br/><br/>Kristen grew up in Brownsburg, Indiana but has lived in Denver, Colorado and the West Country of England. Thus she has been blessed to have friends a</span>
  <span id="freeText15433449007212965080" style="display:none">Kristen Ashley was born in Gary, Indiana, USA. She nearly killed her mother and herself making it into the world, seeing as she had the umbilical cord wrapped around her neck (already attempting to accessorise and she hadn't taken her first breath!). <br /><br />Kristen grew up in Brownsburg, Indiana but has lived in Denver, Colorado and the West Country of England. Thus she has been blessed to have friends and family around the globe. Her posse is loopy (to say the least) but loopy is good when you want to write.<br /><br />Kristen was raised in a house with a large and multi-generational family. They lived on a very small farm in a small town in the heartland and existed amongst the strains of Glenn Miller, The Everly Brothers, REO Speedwagon and Whitesnake (and the wardrobes that matched).<br /><br />Needless to say, growing up in a house full of music, clothes and love was a good way to grow up. <br /><br />And as she keeps growing up, it keeps getting better.</span>
